8: ## Phase 0: Intake & Canonical Foundation
9:
10: Before any architecture is built, the "person-tied" project must gather its raw evidence of existence. This material is often scattered and unformalized.
11:

13: - Text/iMessage transcripts (raw asks, "atomic wants")
14: - Voice call/Zoom transcripts

19: **Action:**
20: 1. Isolate all inputs into an `intakes/` folder.
21: 2. Initialize a local, version-controlled git repository specifically tied to the Organ/domain this person falls under.
22: 3. Establish the base governance files: `seed.yaml`, `AGENTS.md`, `README.md`, `HANDOFF.md`.
23:
24: ---
25:
26: ## Phase 1: Directory Substrate Template
27:
28: Every person-tied client lane must adhere to the following directory structure to maintain cross-system coherence:
29:
30: ```text
31: client-repo/
32: ├── seed.yaml                  # System-readable identity & governance
33: ├── AGENTS.md                  # Context for AI agents (style, commands, boundaries)
34: ├── README.md                  # Human-readable project summary
35: ├── docs/                      # Canonical layer (The Pragma)
36: │   ├── business/              # Strategy, Pitch decks, Funnel specs
37: │   ├── content/               # Social scripts, rituals, pillars
38: │   ├── client-decisions/      # Atomized wants, message extraction, formal approvals
39: │   ├── superpowers/intakes/   # Raw transcripts, exports, text messages
40: │   └── substrate/             # Knowledge graphs, ontology definitions, gap maps
41: ├── src/                       # Application / Delivery layer (if applicable)
42: └── .claude/plans/             # (or .gemini/plans) Persistent execution plans
43: ```
44:
45: ---
46:
47: ## Phase 2: Epistemic Distillation
48:
49: Convert the raw Phase 0 intake into the structured Phase 1 directories.
50:
51: 1. **Persona & Lexicon Extraction**: Identify the client's "power-vocabulary" and define their persona (`~/Documents/personas/[name].md`).
52: 2. **Domain Mapping**: Catalog all physical assets (domain names, external SaaS platforms, affiliate portals).
53: 3. **The Black Hole Ledger**: Explicitly list all "Pending Homework" — items that gate progress and require a physical address/answer from the client.
54: 4. **Drift Identification**: Run the AI systems to find contradictions between what the system claims is true (e.g., "Contract finalized") and what the raw text proves (e.g., "Agreed in principle").
55:
56: ---
57:
58: ## Phase 3: The Warm-Clock Execution Loop
59:
60: Once the substrate is laid and the knowledge is distilled, the project enters the 3-cadence execution loop to prevent state-rot:
61:
62: 1. **Active-Warm (The Builder):**
63:    - Intentional, human-driven sessions focusing on feature delivery, writing, and direct problem-solving.
64: 2. **Daily Drift (The Sentinel):**
65:    - Automated/background passes that diff the raw `intakes/` against the `docs/` and `seed.yaml`. Identifies when the system state has drifted from reality.
66: 3. **On-Demand Orthogonal (The Red-Team):**
67:    - Adversarial AI passes tasked explicitly with proving the current documentation wrong, finding "ghost references," or challenging the architectural assumptions.
68:
69: ---
70:
71: ## Phase 4: Cross-Pollination (Optional)
72:
73: When multiple person-tied lanes exist (e.g., Rob and Maddie), identify abstract concepts that can bridge them. Examples include:
74: - Shared SOPs (e.g., The "Verbatim Extraction" SOP)
75: - Shared conceptual substrates (e.g., "The Gamified Life" applying to both fitness and philosophy)
76: - Shared architectural components (e.g., reusable GoHighLevel funnels or Stripe integration models)
77:
78: **Rule:** Do not merge their repos. Maintain the separation of IP, but cross-pollinate the *systemic knowledge* via the `meta-organvm` central nervous system.

6: # Rob Bonavoglia: Inbound Engine Architecture Spec
7:
8: **Date:** 2026-04-28
9: **Pivot:** Transitioning Rob from Manual SDR ("weed scraping") to Automated Inbound Engine
10:
11: ## 1. The Redteam Diagnosis
12: The previous architecture assumed the BODI "funnel" was a mature, scalable system that could be ported to Hokage Chess. The 2026-04-27 Redteam analysis exposed this as a critical error: the BODI "funnel" is actually a high-touch, 1-to-1 manual sales pipeline reliant on Rob sending Instagram DMs to cold leads. This creates a hard ceiling on scale dictated by Rob's waking hours.
13:
14: ## 2. The Architectural Pivot
15: We are abandoning the attempt to port the manual SDR process. Instead, we must build a true **Organic Inbound Engine** that replaces the Level 1 bottleneck across both brands.
16:
17: ### The New Funnel Flow
18: 1. **Traffic Generation (Organic Inbound)**: SEO / YouTube / POSSE syndication. Rob's energy shifts from 1-to-1 DMs to 1-to-Many content creation.
19: 2. **Landing Page (The Anchor)**: A dedicated, branded landing page replacing the fragile Google Form.
20: 3. **Lead Magnet Delivery (Level 1 → Level 2 Transition)**: Automated email delivery (via Kit) of premium content (e.g., "Road to 1500" PDF guide, exclusive PGNs) upon email capture.
21: 4. **CRM Integration**: Automated lead routing from Kit into Teamzy. Teamzy shifts from being a manual ledger of cold DMs to an intake receiver for warm, qualified leads.
22:
23: ## 3. Operational Requirements
24:
25: ### Infrastructure Needed
26: - **Landing Page Host**: Cloudflare Pages / Vercel (to host the static site).
27: - **Email Service Provider (ESP)**: Kit (formerly ConvertKit) API integration for the email capture form.
28: - **Lead Magnet Asset**: A high-value digital artifact ready for automated delivery.
29:
30: ### Rob's Role Shift
31: - **Stop**: Manually finding and DMing followers on Instagram.
32: - **Start**: Creating Bridge Content (PRT-040) designed to point viewers directly to the new Landing Page URL.

<content>
1: # Spec: Karpathy LLM-Wiki Pattern Adoption for `my-knowledge-base`
2:
3: ## Origin & Context
4: - **Trigger**: Audit of potential system substrates (2026-04-27) flagged Andrej Karpathy's LLM-wiki architecture as a highest-leverage move for `my-knowledge-base`.
5: - **Core Principle**: Shift the complexity of knowledge assembly from "query-time" (traditional RAG) to "compile-time". Instead of retrieving vector-fragmented chunks and relying on the LLM to synthesize them on the fly, the system uses an LLM as a "compiler" to pre-process raw transcripts into a structured, hyperlinked, human-readable wiki.
6:
7: ## Current vs. Target State
8: - **Current State (`my-knowledge-base`)**: Operates on a traditional retrieval paradigm. It atomizes conversations into chunks (`AtomicUnit`), stores them in ChromaDB (semantic) and SQLite FTS5 (keyword), and uses RRF fusion to retrieve them. While it has an LLM Intelligence layer (`InsightExtractor`, `SmartTagger`), it fundamentally retrieves scattered fragments at query-time.
9: - **Target State (Karpathy Pattern)**: A new "Compiler" subsystem that acts on the ingested federated sources to produce a static, interconnected set of markdown documents (the Wiki). Retrieval becomes primarily a navigation task (reading the compiled wiki) rather than a dynamic synthesis task.
10:
11: ## Architectural Additions
12:
13: ### 1. The Wiki Compiler Subsystem
14: Introduce a new `WikiCompiler` class (`src/wiki-compiler/`) that operates sequentially over the corpus.
15: - **Phase A (Topic Extraction & Clustering)**: LLM scans raw conversations and atomic units, clustering them into canonical "Topics" or "Entities".
16: - **Phase B (Page Synthesis)**: For each Topic, the LLM generates a comprehensive, narrative markdown page synthesizing all relevant insights, decisions, and code snippets across the corpus.
17: - **Phase C (Cross-linking)**: The LLM processes the generated pages to inject markdown cross-links (`[Topic B](./topic-b.md)`) whenever a concept is referenced, forming a dense knowledge graph.
18:
19: ### 2. Output Format (The Compiled Wiki)
20: - **Directory Structure**: A static output directory (`/compiled-wiki/`) containing `.md` files.
21: - **Index Generation**: An auto-generated `index.md` serving as the root ontology.
22: - **Integration with ORGAN-V (Logos)**: The compiled markdown files can be directly ingested into Jekyll/Astro sites for public or semi-public distribution, perfectly aligning with POSSE.
23:
24: ### 3. Workflow Modifications
25: - `npm run compile:wiki`: New CLI command to trigger the pipeline.
26: - The pipeline relies heavily on the `BatchProcessor` and `AIFactory` already present, but introduces a multi-step reduce operation (Map raw units -> Reduce to Topic Pages -> Refine links).
27:
28: ## Strategic Leverage
29: 1. **Zero-Latency Retrieval**: The user navigates pre-computed pages instantly.
30: 2. **Higher Quality Synthesis**: The LLM has the full time and context to synthesize a cohesive narrative during the build step, avoiding query-time context window limits and hallucinations.
31: 3. **Artifact Portability**: The output is just markdown files, deeply compatible with Obsidian, GitHub, and standard SSGs.

(End of file - total 31 lines)
</content>

<system-reminder>
Instructions from: /Users/4jp/Workspace/organvm/my-knowledge-base/AGENTS.md
# Repository Guidelines

Global policy: /Users/4jp/AGENTS.md applies and cannot be overridden.

## Project Structure & Module Organization
- `src/` contains the TypeScript application logic: services, features, API handlers, and phase-specific modules.
- `tests/` provides higher-level Vitest suites that exercise API contracts; unit tests sit next to implementation files in `src/*.test.ts`.
- `web/` hosts the React-based UI, `docs/` holds contributing/operations guides, and `scripts/` automates local workflows (backup, migration, export).
- Data and generated artifacts live under `db/`, `raw/`, `atomized/`, and `dist/` once builds are emitted.
- Keep service code modular by following the current capability grouping (e.g., search, analytics, admin) so features remain discoverable.

## Build, Test, and Development Commands
- `npm run dev` runs the TypeScript server with hot reload for rapid iteration.
- `npm run build` compiles everything into `dist/`; `npm run start` launches the compiled output.
- `npm run test` executes Vitest suites, while `npm run test:coverage` collects coverage reports and `npm run test:ui` validates UI helpers.
- UI-specific tasks include `npm run web` (starts the React app) and `npm run backup` (triggers backup automation; `BACKUP_ENCRYPT=true` enables encryption).
- Database helpers: `npm run migrate` applies schema changes and `npm run seed` populates sample data; invoke `npm run migrate && npm run seed` before running the web server or tests when schema drift is suspected.

## Coding Style & Naming Conventions
- TypeScript, ESM modules, and `strict` mode per `tsconfig.json`; prefer 2-space indentation and semicolons.
- Files use kebab-case, classes use PascalCase, and functions/variables follow camelCase.
- Emphasize small services with clear responsibility (e.g., `smart-tagger.ts`, `insight-extractor.ts`) to keep imports readable.
- Run formatting/linting via `npm run lint` when adding code; matching existing patterns is critical for maintainability.

## Testing Guidelines
- Vitest is the default runner; keep tests close to sources using `*.test.ts`.
- Name suites to match their feature (e.g., `src/semantic-chunker.test.ts`) and update fixtures when schema changes touch analytics or API behavior.
- Reuse existing mocks for Claude/OpenAI APIs to avoid flakiness; ensure rate-limit and token-stat assertions align with the injected delays.

## Commit & Pull Request Guidelines
- Commit messages follow Conventional Commits (`feat:`, `fix:`, `docs:`, `chore:`).
- PRs should include a short summary, list of tests run, and links to related issues or cards; include screenshots for UI work (`web/`) when relevant.
- Keep generated files out of VCS unless part of a documented workflow (`db/` dumps require justification).

## Deployment & Operation Notes
- Documented workflows reside in `CONTRIBUTING.md` and `docs/OPERATIONS.md`; link to them when adding new automation.
- CI should run `npm run migrate && npm run seed` before tests to keep analytic suites stable.
- Backup automation runs via `npm run backup`; a passing review mentions whether encryption (`BACKUP_ENCRYPT=true`) was exercised.

250:     *   `organvm-iii-ergon/hokage-chess` (This current repo: Organ III / Commerce / Work)
251:     *   `a-organvm/gamified-coach-interface` (The sister repo: Legion Command Center)
252:     *   `organvm-iv-taxis/orchestration-start-here` (Organ IV: Order / Orchestration)
253:     *   `organvm-vi-koinonia/community-hub` (Organ VI: Community)
254:     *   `organvm-vii-kerygma/social-automation` (Organ VII: Messaging)
255:     *   `meta-organvm/organvm-corpvs-testamentvm/` (The meta-registry that tracks the entire "body" of the system)
256: *   **The Directory/File:** `seed.yaml` in the root directory.
257: *   **Pointing to the Value:** The `seed.yaml` file explicitly maps this specific repository to the overarching organism with the values: `organ: PERSONAL`, `tier: standard`, `type: client-project`.
258:
259: ### 2. The Human's "Perfect Being" (The Character Sheet & Stats)
260: To be a "perfect being" in this gamified system, a human must max out their skill trees and overcome their "debuffs." This has been explicitly ported into the code via the landing page engine.
261: *   **The Deepest Nested Directory:** `src/lib/landing-engine/`
262: *   **The File:** `src/lib/landing-engine/personas.ts`
263: *   **Pointing to the Value (The Types & Functions):**
264:     The code explicitly defines the 6 "pillars" (the stats needed to form a complete player/person) and maps the pain points (debuffs) to the personas.
265:     ```typescript
266:     // The "Stats" required to become a complete player
267:     export type PillarId =
268:       | "tactics"
269:       | "strategy"
270:       | "calculation"
271:       | "endgame"
272:       | "time-management"
273:       | "tilt-resistance";
274:     ```
275:     The exact function that returns the completed archetypes literally "points to the value":
276:     ```typescript
277:     export function listPersonas(): Persona[] {
278:       return Object.values(PERSONAS); // <-- Points to the value of the completed personas
279:     }
280:     ```
281:
282: ### 3. The Business's "Perfect Being" (The Substrate & Knowledge Graph)
283: A business reaches its "Apex" state when it perfectly maps its reality and covers all its blind spots (gaps).
284: *   **The Deepest Nested Directories:**
285:     *   `docs/substrate/bodi/01-ontology/`
286:     *   `docs/substrate/bodi/04-gap-map/`
287: *   **The Files:**
288:     *   `docs/substrate/bodi/01-ontology/bodi-knowledge-graph.json`
289:     *   `docs/substrate/bodi/04-gap-map/heist-targets.yaml`
290: *   **Pointing to the Value:**
291:     The `bodi-knowledge-graph.json` maps the entire "brain" of the business by linking the operator (Rob) to the exact stages of the funnel (`l0-content` -> `l4-ambassador`). The `heist-targets.yaml` file points to the specific values (outcomes) needed to close the missing gaps and make the system whole (e.g., `outcome: Categorized library of 100+ reels/shorts for reuse`).
292:
293: **User >**
294: You are requested to export the session history.
295:
296: **Usage:** `/history:export [format]` (default: markdown)
297:
298: **Instructions:**
299: 1.  Follow the **Export Protocol** defined in `GEMINI.md`.
300: 2.  Calculate the project hash to locate the history files.
301: 3.  Find the latest session file in `~/.gemini/tmp/<HASH>/chats/`.
302: 4.  Read the JSON content.
303: 5.  Convert it to the requested format (Markdown, JSON, or CSV).
304: 6.  Write the result to a new file in the current directory.
305: 7.  Confirm the filename to the user.

190: │                                                                                                                 │
191: │ You can use the list (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files/list) method on │
192: │ the                                                                                                             │
193: │ files (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files) resource to return all or     │

196: │ used to retrieve the fileId required for some resource methods (such as the                                     │
197: │ get (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files/get) method and the update       │

199: │                                                                                                                 │
200: │ Use the fields parameter                                                                                        │
201: │                                                                                                                 │
202: │ If you want to specify the fields to return in the response, you can set the                                    │
203: │ fields [system                                                                                                  │
204: │ parameter](https://cloud.google.com/apis/docs/system-parameters#definitions)                                    │
205: │ with any method of the files resource. If you omit the fields parameter, the                                    │
206: │ server returns a default set of fields specific to the method. For example, the                                 │
207: │ list (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files/list) method returns only the   │
208: │ kind, id,                                                                                                       │
209: │ name, mimeType, and resourceKey fields for each file. To return different                                       │
210: │ fields, see Return specific fields (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/fields-parameter). │
211: │                                                                                                                 │
212: │ Get a file                                                                                                      │
213: │                                                                                                                 │
214: │ To get a file, use the get (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files/get)      │
215: │ method on the                                                                                                   │
216: │ files (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files) resource with the fileId path │
217: │ parameter.                                                                                                      │
218: │ If you don't know the file ID, you can list all files                                                           │
219: │ (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/search-files#all) using the list                      │
220: │ method.                                                                                                         │
221: │                                                                                                                 │
222: │ The method returns the file as an instance of a files resource. If you provide                                  │
223: │ the alt=media query parameter, then the response includes the file contents in                                  │
224: │ the response body. To download or export the file, see [Download and export                                     │
225: │ files](https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/manage-downloads).                              │
226: │                                                                                                                 │

228: │ abusive (https://support.google.com/docs/answer/148505) files, set the                                          │

230: │ the alt=media parameter is set and the user is either the file owner or an                                      │

232: │                                                                                                                 │
233: │ Search for all files and folders on the current user's My Drive                                                 │
234: │                                                                                                                 │
235: │ Use the list method without any parameters to return all files and folders.                                     │
236: │                                                                                                                 │
237: │     GET https://www.googleapis.com/drive/v3/files                                                               │
238: │                                                                                                                 │
239: │ Search for specific files or folders on the current user's My Drive                                             │
240: │                                                                                                                 │
241: │ To search for a specific set of files or folders, use the query string q field                                  │
242: │ with the list (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files/list) method to filter │
243: │ the files to                                                                                                    │
244: │ return by combining one or more search terms.                                                                   │
245: │                                                                                                                 │
246: │ The query string syntax contains the following three parts:                                                     │
247: │                                                                                                                 │
248: │ query_term operator values                                                                                      │
249: │                                                                                                                 │
250: │ Where:                                                                                                          │
251: │                                                                                                                 │
252: │  - query_term is the query term or field to search upon.                                                        │
253: │                                                                                                                 │
254: │  - operator specifies the condition for the query term.                                                         │
255: │                                                                                                                 │
256: │  - values are the specific values you want to use to filter your search                                         │
257: │   results.                                                                                                      │
258: │                                                                                                                 │
259: │ For example, the following query string filters the search to only return                                       │
260: │ folders by setting the MIME type (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/mime-types):         │
261: │                                                                                                                 │
262: │     q: mimeType = 'application/vnd.google-apps.folder'                                                          │
263: │                                                                                                                 │
264: │ To view all file query terms, see File-specific query terms                                                     │
265: │ (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/ref-search-terms#file-properties).                    │
266: │                                                                                                                 │
267: │ To view all query operators that you can use to construct a query, see [Query                                   │
268: │ operators](https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/ref-search-terms#operators).                │
269: │                                                                                                                 │
270: │ Query string examples                                                                                           │
271: │                                                                                                                 │
272: │ The following table lists examples of some basic query strings. The actual code                                 │
273: │ differs depending on the client library you use for your search.                                                │
274: │                                                                                                                 │
275: │ > [!IMPORTANT]                                                                                                  │
276: │ > Important: The following query terms use fields from the [Drive API                                           │
277: │ > v3](https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3). Some resource fields changed        │
278: │ between v2 and v3. For example, name replaces title. If you're using [Drive API                                 │
279: │ > v2](https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v2), adjust these queries to use the v2  │
280: │ fields. For more information, see [Drive API v2 and v3 comparison                                               │
281: │ > reference](https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/v2-to-v3-reference).                      │
282: │                                                                                                                 │
283: │ You must also escape special characters in your file names to make sure the                                     │
284: │ query works correctly. For example, if a filename contains both an apostrophe                                   │
285: │ (') and a backslash ("\") character, use a backslash to escape them: `name                                      │
286: │ contains 'quinn\'s paper\\essay'`.                                                                              │

289: │ > Note: These examples use the unencoded q parameter, where name = 'hello' is encoded as name+%3d+%27hello%27.  │
290: │ Client libraries handle this encoding automatically.                                                            │
291: │                                                                                                                 │
292: │ ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┐   │
293: │ │ What you want to query                                             │ Example                              │   │
294: │ ├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────┤   │
295: │ │ Files with the name "hello"                                        │ name = 'hello'                       │   │

297: │ │                                                                    │ contains 'goodbye'                   │   │

300: │ │                                                                    │ trashed = true                       │   │

302: │ │ Files that don't have the word "hello"                             │ not fullText contains 'hello'        │   │
303: │ │ Files that contain the exact phrase "hello world"                  │ fullText contains '"hello world"'    │   │
304: │ │ Files with a query that contains the "\\" character (for example,  │ fullText contains '\\authors'        │   │
305: │ │ "\\authors")                                                       │                                      │   │

450:
451:   2. Finding files using the Google Workspace Drive API
452:   If you are referring to searching the organization's domain programmatically using the Google Drive API, I've checked
453:   the latest Workspace documentation on how to achieve this.
454:
455:   To search for all files shared with a specific domain, you use the files.list
456:   (https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/files/list) method and explicitly set the
457:   corpora query parameter to "domain".
458:
459:   Here is an example in Node.js:
460:
461:    1 const result = await service.files.list({
462:    2   corpora: 'domain',
463:    3   // Optional: narrow it down further with a query (e.g. by mimeType)
464:    4   // q: "mimeType='application/vnd.google-apps.document'",
465:    5   fields: 'nextPageToken, files(id, name)',
466:    6 });
467:
468:   Note: By default, the corpora parameter is set to user. When searching a large domain, you will need to handle
469:   pagination using nextPageToken, and the API might return an incompleteSearch: true flag in the response body if the
470:   item collection is too large to resolve completely.

# AGENTS.md

This file provides guidance for AI coding agents operating in this repository.

## Project Overview

**Sovereign Systems Spiral** — multi-domain Astro 5 website for client Maddie's 4-pillar health and business brand. Hub-and-spoke architecture with `elevatealign.com` as central hub, `stopdrinkingacid.com` for Water/Physical Sovereignty, and `eaucohub.com` for Financial Sovereignty.

- **Organ:** III (Commerce / Ergon)
- **Client IP boundary:** content = client's IP (do not distribute or reuse); code/architecture = studio IP

## Tech Stack

- **Astro 5** — static site generator, zero JS by default
- **Tailwind CSS 4** — via `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin (CSS-first config, no `tailwind.config.js`)
- **TypeScript** — strict mode, no `any`
- **Vanilla Canvas** — `src/components/spiral/spiral.ts` drives animated spiral (no Three.js, no external canvas libs)

---

## Build & Dev Commands

```bash
npm run dev        # Dev server at localhost:4321
npm run build      # Production build → dist/
npm run preview    # Preview production build locally
npm run parse-citations  # Parse citations from source documents
```

### Running a Single Test

**No test framework is currently configured.** To add tests:

```bash
# Install testing dependencies
npm install -D vitest @testing-library/astro jsdom

# Run tests
npx vitest run
npx vitest run src/components/spiral/spiral.test.ts  # Run single file
npx vitest --watch src/components/spiral/            # Watch mode
```

### Linting

**No linter is currently configured.** To add linting:

```bash
# Install ESLint and related packages
npm install -D eslint @eslint/astro eslint-plugin-astro typescript-eslint

# Run lint
npx eslint src/
```

---

## Code Style Guidelines

### General Principles

- Write clear, readable code over clever code
- Use descriptive names for variables, functions, classes
- Keep functions small and focused (single responsibility)
- Prefer composition over inheritance
- Don't repeat yourself (DRY), but avoid premature abstraction

### TypeScript Conventions

- **Always use strict TypeScript** — no `any` allowed
- Use explicit return types for public functions
- Prefer interfaces over types for object shapes
- Use proper TypeScript utility types when needed (`ReturnType`, `Partial`, etc.)
- Define types in `.ts` files, not inline

```typescript
// Good
interface PillarData {
  name: string;
  slug: string;
  emoji: string;
  color: string;
  status: 'live' | 'coming-soon';
}

function initSpiral(canvas: HTMLCanvasElement, pillars: PillarData[]): () => void {
  // ...
}
```

### Naming Conventions

| Element | Convention | Example |
|---------|------------|---------|
| Variables | camelCase | `baseRadius`, `nodeStates` |
| Functions | camelCase | `initNoise()`, `drawOrbitalPaths()` |
| Interfaces/Types | PascalCase | `PillarData`, `HubConfig` |
| Constants | SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE | `BASE_ROTATION_SPEED` |
| Astro components | PascalCase | `SpiralIsland.astro` |
| Files (components) | PascalCase | `spiral.ts` → fine for utilities |

### Imports & Exports

- Use named exports for all exports (no default exports)
- Group imports logically: external packages → internal modules → types
- Use absolute imports from `@/` alias when available

```typescript
import type { PillarData } from '../data/hub.config';
import { config } from '../data/hub.config';
```

### Formatting

- Use 2 spaces for indentation
- Maximum line length: 100 characters
- Use trailing commas in arrays and objects
- Use semicolons for statement termination

### Error Handling

- Handle errors explicitly with meaningful messages
- Fail fast on invalid inputs
- Use try/catch for async operations with proper error propagation
- Never swallow errors silently

```typescript
function hexToRgba(hex: string, alpha: number): string {
  if (!hex.startsWith('#') || hex.length !== 7) {
    throw new Error(`Invalid hex color: ${hex}`);
  }
  // ...
}
```

### Astro Components

- Use `.astro` files for static content and island wrappers
- Prefer `client:idle` or `client:visible` for hydration (avoid `client:load` unless necessary)
- Provide SVG fallbacks for Canvas/JS-dependent components
- Use content collections (`src/content/`) for Markdown content with frontmatter

### Tailwind CSS 4

- No `tailwind.config.js` — use CSS-first configuration
- Define custom properties and theme in global CSS
- Use `@theme` directive for custom design tokens
- Keep utility classes in components, extract to globals only for truly reusable patterns

```css
/* src/styles/global.css */
@theme {
  --color-brand: #119a9e;
  --font-family-display: 'Inter', system-ui, sans-serif;
}
```

### Canvas & Animation

- Target 60fps for animations
- Use `requestAnimationFrame` for render loops
- Implement proper cleanup functions to prevent memory leaks
- Provide static fallbacks for no-JS environments
- Handle DPR (device pixel ratio) for crisp rendering

```typescript
return function cleanup(): void {
  cancelAnimationFrame(animFrame);
  window.removeEventListener('resize', resize);
  canvas.removeEventListener('mousemove', updateMouse);
};
```

---

## Project Structure

```
src/
├── components/
│   └── spiral/
│       ├── spiral.ts          # Canvas animation (vanilla TS)
│       ├── SpiralIsland.astro # Astro island wrapper
│       └── SpiralFallback.astro # Static SVG fallback
├── content/
│   ├── branches/              # 6 branch Markdown files
│   └── pillars/               # 3 pillar placeholder pages
├── data/
│   └── hub.config.ts          # Single source of truth for config
├── layouts/
│   └── Base.astro             # Root HTML layout
├── pages/
│   ├── index.astro            # Hub homepage
│   ├── pillars/[slug].astro   # Dynamic pillar pages
│   ├── water/                  # Physical Sovereignty funnel
│   └── business/               # Financial Sovereignty landing
└── styles/
    └── global.css             # Global styles + Tailwind
```

---

## Content Management

- Edit Markdown files in `src/content/` for copy changes
- Update pillar metadata (taglines, colors, URLs) in `src/data/hub.config.ts`
- Frontmatter schema is enforced by `src/content.config.ts`
- To add a new branch: create `src/content/branches/<slug>.md` with correct frontmatter, then add entry to `hub.config.ts`

---

## Deployment

- **Platform:** Cloudflare Pages
- **Build command:** `npm run build` → outputs to `dist/`
- **Functions:** `functions/capture.ts` for email capture
- Primary domain: `elevatealign.com`
- Auto-deploy on push to `main`

---

## Session Guidelines

- Mirror canonical handoffs into `docs/` before treating as authoritative
- Keep dated artifacts in `docs/superpowers/intakes/` and `.codex/plans/`
- If scope or board state changes, reconcile `seed.yaml` and `CLAUDE.md` in the same session
- Commit and push before close for project memory persistence

625:        1 # Implementation Plan: Omega — Total Loop Closure & Launch
626:        2
627:        3 ## Background & Motivation
628:        4 We have reached the final 1% of the Maddie Spiral development
629:          cycle. The corpus has been atomized (1,821 source atoms + 241
630:          prompt atoms), the 3D helix is operational, and the revenue
631:          agreement is finalized. This plan serves as the "Omega"
632:          directive to address the final conceptual gaps (Non-Profit
633:          narrative, GIS Map integration) and execute the technical
634:          handoff.
635:        5
636:        6 ## Scope & Impact
637:        7 This plan covers:
638:        8 1.  **Conceptual Integration:** Infusing "Non-Profit" and
639:          "Sovereign Giving" narratives into the content collections.
640:        9 2.  **Visual "Map of Earth" Layer:** Integrating a conceptual
641:          GIS/Cartographic layer into the 3D Three.js spiral to satisfy
642:          the "literal map of earth history" directive.
643:       10 3.  **Operational Launch:** CI Token rotation, Cloudflare DNS
644:          finalization, and affiliate link wiring.
645:       11 4.  **Total Proof:** Closing the final two "Pending" atoms in
646:          the Prompt Registry.
647:       12
648:       13 ## Proposed Solution & Implementation Steps
649:       14
650:       15 ### Phase 1: Conceptual Fusion (Content)
651:       16 - **Non-Profit Integration:** Update
652:          `src/content/pillars/financial.md` and
653:          `src/content/pillars/identity.md` to include Maddie's specific
654:          language regarding non-profit missions, hidden homelessness
655:          support, and the "10% for the world" model.
656:       17 - **Evidence:** Atom PRMPT-ATM-219 moves to `Implemented`.
657:       18
658:       19 ### Phase 2: The "Fossil Record" Layer (3D Visuals)
659:       20 - **GIS Visual Layer:** Modify `src/components/spiral/spiral.ts`
660:          to add a secondary, low-opacity "point cloud" or "wireframe
661:          sphere" layer within the helix that represents cartographic
662:          coordinates.
663:       21 - **Atmospheric Change:** Use a "parchment/old-world" color
664:          palette (#d4c4a8) for these coordinate points to simulate the
665:          "cartographical fossil record."
666:       22 - **Evidence:** Atom PRMPT-ATM-224 moves to `Implemented`.
667:       23
668:       24 ### Phase 3: Launch-Critical Surfaces (Technical)
669:       25 - **CI Token Rotation:** Generate a new Cloudflare Scoped API
670:          Token. (Action: Manual update of GH Secret
671:          `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`).
672:       26 - **Affiliate Wire-up:** Update `src/data/hydration.config.ts`
673:          with placeholder-to-live mapping for IonFaucet/Multipure.
674:       27 - **GHL Bridge:** Final test of the `capture.ts` function
675:          against a live GHL webhook endpoint.
676:       28
677:       29 ### Phase 4: Final Verification & Audit
678:       30 - Run `npm run build` one last time.
679:       31 - Perform a "hall-monitor" audit of the `dist/` output to ensure
680:          all 263 citations and 13 nodes are present and reactive.
681:       32 - Update the Prompt Atom Registry fidelity score to 100%.
682:       33
683:       34 ## Alternatives Considered
684:       35 - *Ignoring the Map Concept:* We could leave the spiral as is,
685:          but the user explicitly requested a "real fucking map of earth
686:          history." Adding a subtle coordinate-based point cloud satisfies
687:          this without bloating the bundle.
688:       36
689:       37 ## Verification

691:       39 - 3D Helix shows the new cartographic coordinate layer.
692:       40 - All "Pending" items in
693:          `docs/reports/2026-04-27-prompt-atom-registry.md` are marked

695:       41
696:       42 ## Migration & Rollback
